{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_015b6KSTyR6VcTibTJHaCPEy","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # `client-go` Architecture\\n2: \\n3: This document explains the internal architecture of `client-go` for contributors. It describes the\\n4: major components, how they interact, and the key design decisions that shape the library.\\n5: \\n6: ## Client Configuration\\n7: \\n8: There is an architectural separation between loading client configuration and using it. The\\n9: `rest.Config` object is the in-memory representation of this configuration. The\\n10: `tools/clientcmd` package is the standard factory for producing it. `clientcmd` handles the\\n11: complex logic of parsing `kubeconfig` files, merging contexts, and handling external\\n12: authentication providers (e.g., OIDC).\\n13: \\n14: ## REST Client\\n15: \\n16: The `rest.Client` is the foundational HTTP client that underpins all other clients. It separates\\n17: the low-level concerns of HTTP transport, serialization, and error handling from higher-level,\\n18: Kubernetes-specific object logic.\\n19: \\n20: The `rest.Config` object is used to build the underlying HTTP transport, which is typically a\\n21: chain of `http.RoundTripper` objects. Each element in the chain is responsible for a specific\\n22: task, such as adding an `Authorization` header. This is the mechanism by which all authentication\\n23: is injected into requests.\\n24: \\n25: The client uses a builder pattern for requests (e.g., `.Verb()`, `.Resource()`), deferring\\n26: response processing until a method like `.Into(&pod)` is called. This separation is key to\\n27: supporting different client models from a common base.\\n28: \\n29: ### Endpoint Interactions\\n30: \\n31: *   **Content Negotiation:** The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate the wire format\\n32:     (JSON or Protobuf). A key performance optimization using this mechanism is the ability to\\n33:     request metadata-only objects via the `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameter.\\n34:     Also the `as=Table;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameters may be used to request lists as tables. \\n35: *   **Subresources:** The client can target standard subresources like `/status` or `/scale` for\\n36:     object mutations, and it can also handle action-oriented subresources like `/logs` or\\n37:     `/exec`, which often involve streaming data.\\n38: *   **List Pagination:** For `LIST` requests, the client can specify a `limit`. The server will\\n39:     return up to that many items and, if more exist, a `continue` token. The client is\\n40:     responsible for passing this token in a subsequent request to retrieve the next page.\\n41:     Higher-level tools like the `Reflector`'s `ListerWatcher` handle this logic automatically.\\n42: *   **Streaming Watches:** A `WATCH` request returns a `watch.Interface` (from\\n43:     `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/watch`), which provides a channel of structured `watch.Event`\\n44:     objects (`ADDED`, `MODIFIED`, `DELETED`, `BOOKMARK`). This decouples the watch consumer from\\n45:     the underlying streaming protocol.\\n46: \\n47: ### Errors, Warnings, and Rate Limiting\\n48: \\n49: *   **Structured Errors:** The client deserializes non-2xx responses into a structured\\n50:     `errors.StatusError`, enabling programmatic error handling (e.g., `errors.IsNotFound(err)`).\\n51: *   **Warnings:** It processes non-fatal `Warning` headers from the API server via a\\n52:     `WarningHandler`.\\n53: *   **Client-Side Rate Limiting:** The `QPS` and `Burst` settings in `rest.Config` are the\\n54:     client's half of the contract with the server's API Priority and Fairness system.\\n55: *   **Server-Side Throttling:** The client's default transport automatically handles HTTP `429`\\n56:     responses by reading the `Retry-After` header, waiting, and retrying the request.\\n57: \\n58: ## Typed and Dynamic Clients\\n59: \\n60: To handle the extensible nature of the Kubernetes API, `client-go` provides two primary client\\n61: models.\\n62: \\n63: The **`kubernetes.Clientset`** provides compile-time, type-safe access to core, built-in APIs.\\n64: \\n65: The **`dynamic.DynamicClient`** represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, allowing it\\n66: to interact with any API resource, including CRDs. It relies on two discovery mechanisms:\\n67: 1.  The **`discovery.DiscoveryClient`** determines *what* resources exist. The\\n68:     **`CachedDiscoveryClient`** is an optimization that caches this data on disk to solve.\\n69: 2.  The **OpenAPI schema** (fetched from `/openapi/v3`) describes the *structure* of those\\n70:     resources, providing the schema awareness needed by the dynamic client.\\n71: \\n72: ## Code Generation\\n73: \\n74: A core architectural principle of `client-go` is the use of code generation to provide a\\n75: strongly-typed, compile-time-safe interface for specific API GroupVersions. This makes\\n76: controller code more robust and easier to maintain. The tools in `k8s.io/code-generator` produce\\n77: several key components:\\n78: \\n79: *   **Typed Clientsets:** The primary interface for interacting with a specific GroupVersion.\\n80: *   **Typed Listers:** The read-only, cached accessors used by controllers.\\n81: *   **Typed Informers:** The machinery for populating the cache for a specific type.\\n82: *   **Apply Configurations:** The type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\\n83: \\n84: A contributor modifying a built-in API type **must** run the code generation scripts to update all\\n85: of these dependent components. For the Kubernetes project, `hack/update-codegen.sh` runs code generation.\\n86: \\n87: `sample-controller` shows how code generate can be configured to build custom controllers.\\n88: \\n89: ## Controller Infrastructure\\n90: \\n91: The `tools/cache` package provides the core infrastructure for controllers, replacing a high-load,\\n92: request-based pattern with a low-load, event-driven, cached model.\\n93: \\n94: The data flow is as follows:\\n95: \\n96: ```mermaid\\n97: graph TD\\n98:     subgraph \\\"Kubernetes API\\\"\\n99:         API_Server[API Server]\\n100:     end\\n101: \\n102:     subgraph \\\"client-go: Informer Mechanism\\\"\\n103:         Reflector(\\\"1. Reflector\\\")\\n104:         DeltaFIFO(\\\"2. DeltaFIFO\\\")\\n105:         Indexer[\\\"3. Indexer (Cache)\\\"]\\n106:         EventHandlers(\\\"4. Event Handlers\\\")\\n107:     end\\n108: \\n109:     subgraph \\\"User Code\\\"\\n110:         WorkQueue[\\\"5. Work Queue\\\"]\\n111:         Controller(\\\"6. Controller\\\")\\n112:     end\\n113: \\n114:     API_Server -- LIST/WATCH --> Reflector\\n115:     Reflector -- Puts changes into --> DeltaFIFO\\n116:     DeltaFIFO -- Is popped by internal loop, which updates --> Indexer\\n117:     Indexer -- Update triggers --> EventHandlers\\n118:     EventHandlers -- Adds key to --> WorkQueue\\n119:     WorkQueue -- Is processed by --> Controller\\n120:     Controller -- Reads from cache via Lister --> Indexer\\n121: ```\\n122: \\n123: A **`Reflector`** performs a `LIST` to get a consistent snapshot of a resource, identified by a\\n124: `resourceVersion`. It then starts a `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion` to receive a continuous\\n125: stream of subsequent changes. The `Reflector`'s relist/rewatch loop is designed to solve the\\n126: **\\\"too old\\\" `resourceVersion` error** by re-listing. To make this recovery more efficient, the\\n127: `Reflector` consumes **watch bookmarks** from the server, which provide a more recent\\n128: `resourceVersion` to restart from.\\n129: \\n130: The **`Lister`** is the primary, read-only, thread-safe interface for a controller's business\\n131: logic to access the `Indexer`'s cache.\\n132: \\n133: ## Controller Patterns\\n134: \\n135: The controller infrastructure is architecturally decoupled from the controller's business logic to\\n136: ensure resiliency.\\n137: \\n138: The **`util/workqueue`** creates a critical boundary between event detection (the informer's job)\\n139: and reconciliation (the controller's job). Informer event handlers only add an object's key to the\\n140: work queue. This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\\n141: blocking the informer's watch stream.\\n142: \\n143: For high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\\n144: solution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\\n145: shared `Lease` object.\\n146: \\n147: ## Server-Side Apply\\n148: \\n149: `client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\\n150: server's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\\n151: model that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\\n152: **`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\\n153: construct the declarative patch.\\n154: \\n155: ## Versioning and Compatibility\\n156: \\n157: `client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. A `client-go`\\n158: version `v0.X.Y` corresponds to the Kubernetes version `v1.X.Y`.\\n159: \\n160: The Kubernetes API has strong backward compatibility guarantees: a client built with an older\\n161: version of `client-go` will work with a newer API server. However, the reverse is not guaranteed.\\n162: A contributor must not break compatibility with supported versions of the Kubernetes API server.\\n163: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/ARCHITECTURE.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"bcb00934-5194-4a60-bab0-f0466bc891a9","uuid":"68c466b0-ab75-4ed6-8d3a-ba5decdd5408","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # `client-go` Architecture\\n2: \\n3: This document explains the internal architecture of `client-go` for contributors. This decouples the watch consumer from\n45:     the underlying streaming protocol.\n46: \n47: ### Errors, Warnings, and Rate Limiting\n48: \n49: *   **Structured Errors:** The client deserializes non-2xx responses into a structured\n50:     `errors.StatusError`, enabling programmatic error handling (e.g., `errors.IsNotFound(err)`).\n51: *   **Warnings:** It processes non-fatal `Warning` headers from the API server via a\n52:     `WarningHandler`.\n53: *   **Client-Side Rate Limiting:** The `QPS` and `Burst` settings in `rest.Config` are the\n54:     client's half of the contract with the server's API Priority and Fairness system.\n55: *   **Server-Side Throttling:** The client's default transport automatically handles HTTP `429`\n56:     responses by reading the `Retry-After` header, waiting, and retrying the request.\n57: \n58: ## Typed and Dynamic Clients\n59: \n60: To handle the extensible nature of the Kubernetes API, `client-go` provides two primary client\n61: models.\n62: \n63: The **`kubernetes.Clientset`** provides compile-time, type-safe access to core, built-in APIs.\n64: \n65: The **`dynamic.DynamicClient`** represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, allowing it\n66: to interact with any API resource, including CRDs. It relies on two discovery mechanisms:\n67: 1.  The **`discovery.DiscoveryClient`** determines *what* resources exist. The\n68:     **`CachedDiscoveryClient`** is an optimization that caches this data on disk to solve.\n69: 2.  The **OpenAPI schema** (fetched from `/openapi/v3`) describes the *structure* of those\n70:     resources, providing the schema awareness needed by the dynamic client.\n71: \n72: ## Code Generation\n73: \n74: A core architectural principle of `client-go` is the use of code generation to provide a\n75: strongly-typed, compile-time-safe interface for specific API GroupVersions. This makes\n76: controller code more robust and easier to maintain. The tools in `k8s.io/code-generator` produce\n77: several key components:\n78: \n79: *   **Typed Clientsets:** The primary interface for interacting with a specific GroupVersion.\n80: *   **Typed Listers:** The read-only, cached accessors used by controllers.\n81: *   **Typed Informers:** The machinery for populating the cache for a specific type.\n82: *   **Apply Configurations:** The type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\n83: \n84: A contributor modifying a built-in API type **must** run the code generation scripts to update all\n85: of these dependent components. For the Kubernetes project, `hack/update-codegen.sh` runs code generation.\n86: \n87: `sample-controller` shows how code generate can be configured to build custom controllers.\n88: \n89: ## Controller Infrastructure\n90: \n91: The `tools/cache` package provides the core infrastructure for controllers, replacing a high-load,\n92: request-based pattern with a low-load, event-driven, cached model.\n93: \n94: The data flow is as follows:\n95: \n96: ```mermaid\n97: graph TD\n98:     subgraph \"Kubernetes API\"\n99:         API_Server[API Server]\n100:     end\n101: \n102:     subgraph \"client-go: Informer Mechanism\"\n103:         Reflector(\"1. Reflector\")\n104:         DeltaFIFO(\"2. DeltaFIFO\")\n105:         Indexer[\"3. Indexer (Cache)\"]\n106:         EventHandlers(\"4. Event Handlers\")\n107:     end\n108: \n109:     subgraph \"User Code\"\n110:         WorkQueue[\"5. Work Queue\"]\n111:         Controller(\"6. Controller\")\n112:     end\n113: \n114:     API_Server -- LIST/WATCH --> Reflector\n115:     Reflector -- Puts changes into --> DeltaFIFO\n116:     DeltaFIFO -- Is popped by internal loop, which updates --> Indexer\n117:     Indexer -- Update triggers --> EventHandlers\n118:     EventHandlers -- Adds key to --> WorkQueue\n119:     WorkQueue -- Is processed by --> Controller\n120:     Controller -- Reads from cache via Lister --> Indexer\n121: ```\n122: \n123: A **`Reflector`** performs a `LIST` to get a consistent snapshot of a resource, identified by a\n124: `resourceVersion`. It then starts a `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion` to receive a continuous\n125: stream of subsequent changes. The `Reflector`'s relist/rewatch loop is designed to solve the\n126: **\"too old\" `resourceVersion` error** by re-listing. To make this recovery more efficient, the\n127: `Reflector` consumes **watch bookmarks** from the server, which provide a more recent\n128: `resourceVersion` to restart from.\n129: \n130: The **`Lister`** is the primary, read-only, thread-safe interface for a controller's business\n131: logic to access the `Indexer`'s cache.\n132: \n133: ## Controller Patterns\n134: \n135: The controller infrastructure is architecturally decoupled from the controller's business logic to\n136: ensure resiliency.\n137: \n138: The **`util/workqueue`** creates a critical boundary between event detection (the informer's job)\n139: and reconciliation (the controller's job). Informer event handlers only add an object's key to the\n140: work queue. This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\n141: blocking the informer's watch stream.\n142: \n143: For high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\n144: solution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\n145: shared `Lease` object.\n146: \n147: ## Server-Side Apply\n148: \n149: `client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\n150: server's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\n151: model that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\n152: **`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\n153: construct the declarative patch.\n154: \n155: ## Versioning and Compatibility\n156: \n157: `client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. A `client-go`\n158: version `v0.X.Y` corresponds to the Kubernetes version `v1.X.Y`.\n159: \n160: The Kubernetes API has strong backward compatibility guarantees: a client built with an older\n161: version of `client-go` will work with a newer API server. However, the reverse is not guaranteed.\n162: A contributor must not break compatibility with supported versions of the Kubernetes API server.\n163: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/ARCHITECTURE.md"}}}

[What's included](#whats-included)\n24: - [Versioning](#versioning)\n25:   - [Compatibility: your code <-> client-go](#compatibility-your-code---client-go)\n26:   - [Compatibility: client-go <-> Kubernetes clusters](#compatibility-client-go---kubernetes-clusters)\n27:   - For each `v1.x.y` Kubernetes release, the major version (first digit)\n47: would remain `0`.\n48: \n49: - Bugfixes will result in the patch version (third digit) changing. PRs that are\n50: cherry-picked into an older Kubernetes release branch will result in an update\n51: to the corresponding branch in `client-go`, with a corresponding new tag\n52: changing the patch version.\n53: \n54: #### Branches and tags.\n55: \n56: We will create a new branch and tag for each increment in the minor version\n57: number. We will create only a new tag for each increment in the patch\n58: version number. See [semver](http://semver.org/) for definitions of major,\n59: minor, and patch.\n60: \n61: The HEAD of the master branch in client-go will track the HEAD of the master\n62: branch in the main Kubernetes repo.\n63: \n64: #### Compatibility: your code <-> client-go\n65: \n66: The `v0.x.y` tags indicate that go APIs may change in incompatible ways in\n67: different versions.\n68: \n69: See [INSTALL.md](INSTALL.md) for guidelines on requiring a specific\n70: version of client-go.\n71: \n72: #### Compatibility: client-go <-> Kubernetes clusters\n73: \n74: Since Kubernetes is backwards compatible with clients, older `client-go`\n75: versions will work with many different Kubernetes cluster versions.\n76: \n77: We will backport bugfixes--but not new features--into older versions of\n78: `client-go`.\n79: \n80: \n81: #### Compatibility matrix\n82: \n83: |                               | Kubernetes 1.29 | Kubernetes 1.30 | Kubernetes 1.31 | Kubernetes 1.32 | Kubernetes 1.33 | Kubernetes 1.34 |\n84: | ----------------------------- | --------------- | --------------- | --------------- | --------------- | --------------- | --------------- |\n85: |             | +-              | +-              | +-              | +-              |\n87: | `kubernetes-1.31.0`/`v0.31.0` | +-              | +-              | ✓               | +-              | +-             | +-              |\n92: \n93: Key:\n94: \n95: * `✓` Exactly the same features / API objects in both client-go and the Kubernetes\n96:   version.\n97: * `+` client-go has features or API objects that may not be present in the\n98:   Kubernetes cluster, either due to that client-go has additional new API, or\n99:   that the server has removed old API. (E.g., the clock for the release-2.0 branch started ticking when we\n134: tagged v2.0.0, not when we made the first alpha.) This policy applies to\n135: every version greater than or equal to 2.0.\n136: \n137: #### Why do the 1.4 and 1.5 branch contain top-level folder named after the version?\n138: \n139: For the initial release of client-go, we thought it would be easiest to keep\n140: separate directories for each minor version. Store takes ownership of the list, you should not reference\n70: \t// it after calling this function.\n71: \tReplace([]interface{}, string) error\n72: \n73: \t// Resync is meaningless in the terms appearing here but has\n74: \t// meaning in some implementations that have non-trivial\n75: \t// additional behavior (e.g., DeltaFIFO).\n76: \tResync() error\n77: }\n78: \n79: // TransformingStore is an optional interface that can be implemented by the provided store.\n80: // If implemented on the provided store reflector will use the same transformer in its internal stores.\n81: type TransformingStore interface {\n82: \tReflectorStore\n83: \tTransformer() TransformFunc\n84: }\n85: \n86: // Reflector watches a specified resource and causes all changes to be reflected in the given store.\n87: type Reflector struct {\n88: \t// name identifies this reflector. By default, it will be a file:line if possible.\n89: \tname string\n90: \t// The name of the type we expect to place in the store. The name\n91: \t// will be the stringification of expectedGVK if provided, and the\n92: \t// stringification of expectedType otherwise. It is for display\n93: \t// only, and should not be used for parsing or comparison.\n94: \ttypeDescription string\n95: \t// An example object of the type we expect to place in the store.\n96: \t// Only the type needs to be right, except that when that is\n97: \t// `unstructured.Unstructured` the object's `\"apiVersion\"` and\n98: \t// `\"kind\"` must also be right.\n99: \texpectedType reflect.Type\n100: \t// The GVK of the object we expect to place in the store if unstructured.\n101: \texpectedGVK *schema.GroupVersionKind\n102: \t// The destination to sync up with the watch source\n103: \tstore ReflectorStore\n104: \t// listerWatcher is used to perform lists and watches.\n105: \tlisterWatcher ListerWatcherWithContext\n106: \t// backoff manages backoff of ListWatch\n107: \tbackoffManager wait.BackoffManager\n108: \tresyncPeriod   time.Duration\n109: \t// minWatchTimeout defines the minimum timeout for watch requests.\n110: \tminWatchTimeout time.Duration\n111: \t// clock allows tests to manipulate time\n112: \tclock clock.Clock\n113: \t// paginatedResult defines whether pagination should be forced for list calls.\n114: \t// It is set based on the result of the initial list call.\n115: \tpaginatedResult bool\n116: \t// lastSyncResourceVersion is the resource version token last\n117: \t// observed when doing a sync with the underlying store\n118: \t// it is thread safe, but not synchronized with the underlying store\n119: \tlastSyncResourceVersion string\n120: \t// isLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable is true if the previous list or watch request with\n121: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go%3FL1-120"}}}

An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n44: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n45: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n46: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n47: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n48: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n49: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n50: //\\n51: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n52: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n53: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n54: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n55: //\\n56: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n57: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n58: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n59: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n60: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n61: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n62: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n63: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n64: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n65: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n66: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n67: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n68: // selector.\\n69: //\\n70: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n71: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n72: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n73: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n74: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n75: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n76: //\\n77: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n78: // during `Run()`.\\n79: //\\n80: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n81: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n82: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n83: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n84: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n85: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n86: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n87: //\\n88: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n89: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n90: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n91: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n92: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n93: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n94: //\\n95: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n96: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n97: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n98: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n99: // into its constituent parts.\\n100: //\\n101: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n102: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n103: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n104: //\\n105: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n106: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n107: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n108: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n109: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n110: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n111: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n112: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n113: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n114: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n115: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n116: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n117: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n118: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n119: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n120: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n121: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n122: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n123: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n124: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n125: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n126: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n127: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n128: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n129: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n130: //\\n131: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n132: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n133: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n134: // to something else, for example through a\\n135: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n136: //\\n137: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n138: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n139: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n140: type SharedInformer interface {\\n141: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n142: \\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\\n143: \\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\\n144: \\t// different handlers.\\n145: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\\n146: \\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\\n147: \\t// seen every item in the initial list).\\n148: \\t//\\n149: \\t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\\n150: \\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n151: Because\n121: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n122: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n123: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n124: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n125: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n126: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n127: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n128: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n129: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n130: //\n131: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n132: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n133: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n134: // to something else, for example through a\n135: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n136: //\n137: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n138: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n139: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n140: type SharedInformer interface {\n141: \t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n142: \t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n143: \t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n144: \t// different handlers.\n145: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n146: \t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n147: \t// seen every item in the initial list).\n148: \t//\n149: \t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\n150: \tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-150"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01TCfSAvSj1s5p9AFeEUuPyT","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01JexWg5ZLf1a6JTZzg3HRUV","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Client-go Systems Guide: Advanced Architecture and Operations\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nClient-go is the fundamental Go client library for Kubernetes API interaction and controller development. It abstracts HTTP communication with the Kubernetes API server into a layered architecture comprising four key subsystems: (1) REST-based API access with content negotiation and rate limiting, (2) type-safe clients for built-in APIs (kubernetes.Clientset) and dynamic untyped clients for CRDs, (3) a caching and event-driven informer system powered by watch-based state synchronization, and (4) a work queue and leader election infrastructure for building resilient, distributed controllers. This guide explains the architecture, component interactions, end-to-end control flows, operational tradeoffs, and extension patterns essential for building robust Kubernetes controllers and integrating with the API server.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### 1.1 Purpose and Scope\n\nClient-go serves as the canonical Go library for interacting with Kubernetes clusters. Its core mandate is twofold:\n\n1. **API Access Layer**: Provide a safe, type-checked, and performant interface to the Kubernetes REST API.\n2. **Controller Infrastructure**: Supply the event-driven machinery and tools necessary to build stateful, resilient controllers that manage Kubernetes objects declaratively.\n\nClient-go is positioned between two critical boundaries:\n\n- **Upstream Boundary (Kubernetes API Server)**: Client-go communicates with the apiserver over HTTP/2, consuming `LIST`, `WATCH`, `GET`, `POST`, `PATCH`, and `DELETE` operations. It must handle the apiserver's versioning, deprecation, resource discovery, and rate-limit signals (HTTP `429` with `Retry-After` headers).\n- **Downstream Boundary (Controllers and Tools)**: Controllers, kubectl, kubelets, and custom clients consume client-go's high-level abstractions (Clientsets, Informers, Listers, Work Queues) to interact with Kubernetes state without directly managing HTTP, serialization, or polling logic.\n\n### 1.2 External Dependencies\n\n- **k8s.io/apimachinery**: Core Kubernetes type system, serialization (JSON/Protobuf/CBOR), resource versioning, and the Watch interface.\n- **k8s.io/api**: Kubernetes built-in API types (e.g., Pod, Deployment, Service).\n- **Go standard library**: HTTP client, reflection, channels, sync primitives (mutex, WaitGroup).\n- **Third-party libraries**: OpenAPI schema handling, rate limiting (golang.org/x/time/rate), protobuf serialization.\n\n### 1.3 Architectural Principles\n\nClient-go's design reflects several key principles:\n\n- **Code Generation for Type Safety**: Typed clients, listers, and informers are generated from API type definitions, enabling compile-time safety while reducing manual boilerplate.\n- **Eventual Consistency Model**: The informer cache is eventually consistent with the apiserver; consistency is traded for scalability and resilience to transient network failures.\n- **Decoupled Event Detection from Reconciliation**: Informer event handlers (fast, non-blocking) enqueue work items; a separate work queue allows controllers to reconcile asynchronously with exponential backoff.\n- **Single-Writer Semantics**: Leader election ensures only one controller instance acts as \"leader,\" preventing conflicting writes in a high-availability setup.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 REST Client Subsystem (`rest/`)\n\nThe REST client is the foundational transport layer. All higher-level clients ultimately use `rest.Client` and `rest.Request` for HTTP communication.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `rest/config.go`: `Config` struct holds server address, authentication credentials, TLS settings, QPS/Burst rate limiting, and custom transport wrappers.\n- `rest/client.go`: `RESTClient` encapsulates base URL, API path, negotiated serializer, backoff manager, and rate limiter.\n- `rest/request.go`: `Request` struct implements a fluent builder pattern for constructing requests (`.Verb()`, `.Resource()`, `.Namespace()`, `.Name()`, `.Into()`, `.Do()`).\n- `rest/transport.go`: `TransportFor()` constructs an `http.RoundTripper` chain layering authentication, TLS, compression, and rate limiting.\n\n**Key Concepts**:\n\n1. **Builder Pattern for Requests**: A single `Request` instance defers response processing until `.Do()` or `.Into()` is called, decoupling request assembly from execution.\n   ```\n   client.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", v1.GetOptions{})\n   // Internally translates to:\n   // GET /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod\n   ```\n\n2. **Content Negotiation**: The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate wire format (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR). Optional Accept custom parameters enable metadata-only retrieval (`as=PartialObjectMetadata`) or table-formatted lists (`as=Table`).\n\n3. **Transport Chain (RoundTrippers)**: The `http.RoundTripper` interface allows layered middleware:\n   - Authentication (Bearer token, client certs, OAuth via plugins)\n   - TLS/mTLS configuration\n   - Compression (gzip)\n   - User-Agent and custom header injection\n   - Impersonation (user/group override)\n\n4. **Rate Limiting and Backoff**:\n   - **Client-side**: `Config.QPS` (default 5) and `Config.Burst` (default 10) define a token bucket rate limiter enforced at request time.\n   - **Server-side**: The apiserver may return HTTP `429 Too Many Requests`. The client's default transport reads the `Retry-After` header and automatically retries with exponential backoff (capped at 1000 seconds).\n\n### 2.2 Configuration and Authentication (`rest/config.go`, `tools/clientcmd/`)\n\nLoading cluster credentials and constructing a `rest.Config` is logically separated from using it.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `rest/config.go`: `Config` struct and factory functions (`NewDefaultClientConfig()`, `InClusterConfig()`, `BuildConfigFromFlags()`).\n- `tools/clientcmd/`: Parses kubeconfig files, merges contexts, and applies external authentication providers (OIDC, exec-based auth).\n\n**Authentication Flows**:\n- **In-Cluster**: Uses a service account token mounted at `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/token` and the apiserver URL from environment variables.\n- **Out-of-Cluster**: Reads `~/.kube/config` (kubeconfig file) containing cluster, context, and user information.\n- **Exec Plugins**: External commands (e.g., cloud provider SDKs) supply credentials dynamically, refreshed on each request if needed.\n\n### 2.3 Typed Clients: The Clientset (`kubernetes/`)\n\nFor built-in Kubernetes API types, code generation produces `kubernetes.Clientset`, a hierarchical interface providing type-safe access.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `kubernetes/clientset.go`: Generated file (DO NOT EDIT comment) that defines `Clientset` with methods like `.CoreV1()`, `.AppsV1()`, `.BatchV1()`, etc., each returning a versioned client.\n- `kubernetes/typed/*/`: Generated typed clients for each API group version (e.g., `kubernetes/typed/core/v1/` contains Pod, Service, ConfigMap clients).\n\n**Structure**:\n```go\ntype Clientset interface {\n    CoreV1() corev1.CoreV1Interface\n    AppsV1() appsv1.AppsV1Interface\n    // ... other API group methods\n}\n\n// Usage:\npods := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\")\npod, err := pods.Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", v1.GetOptions{})\n```\n\nEach typed client's methods (Create, Update, Patch, Delete, List, Watch, Get) return `rest.Request` objects that defer execution until `.Do()` or `.Into()` is called.\n\n**Code Generation**: Files in `kubernetes/typed/` are auto-generated by `code-generator` tools when API types change. Contributors must run `hack/update-codegen.sh` to stay synchronized.\n\n### 2.4 Dynamic Client (`dynamic/`)\n\nFor Custom Resource Definitions (CRDs) or unknown API resources, the dynamic client operates on `unstructured.Unstructured` (a generic map-based representation) without compile-time type information.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `dynamic/interface.go`: `Interface` defines `.Resource(schema.GroupVersionResource)` returning a `NamespaceableResourceInterface`.\n- `dynamic/simple.go`: Implementation using REST client and OpenAPI schema introspection.\n\n**Key Difference from Typed Clients**:\n- Typed clients: Type-safe, IDE auto-completion, compile-time error detection.\n- Dynamic clients: Flexible, works with any resource, but requires runtime schema validation.\n\n**Resource Discovery**: The dynamic client internally uses `discovery.DiscoveryClient` to list available API resources and `openapi3` schemas to validate fields and marshal/unmarshal objects correctly.\n\n### 2.5 API Discovery (`discovery/`)\n\nThe discovery client introspects the apiserver to enumerate available resources, versions, and OpenAPI schemas.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `discovery/discovery_client.go`: `DiscoveryClient` with methods like `ServerGroups()`, `ServerResourcesForGroupVersion()`, `OpenAPISchema()`, `OpenAPIV3Schema()`.\n- `discovery/cached_discovery.go`: `CachedDiscoveryClient` caches discovery data on disk (by default in `~/.kube/cache/`) to reduce apiserver load.\n\n**Two-Level Discovery**:\n1. **API Resource Discovery** (traditional, v1): Calls `/api` and `/apis` endpoints, returning lists of resource types and their verbs (create, list, watch, delete, etc.).\n2. **Aggregated Discovery** (v2beta1+): A single endpoint returning discovery data for all API groups at once, reducing chatiness and enabling peer-to-peer discovery.\n\n**OpenAPI Schemas**: The OpenAPI endpoint (e.g., `/openapi/v3/apis/v1/...`) provides field descriptions, validation rules, and type information, enabling dynamic client field validation and intelligent table formatting.\n\n### 2.6 Informers and Shared Caches (`tools/cache/`, `informers/`)\n\nThe informer system is client-go's most complex subsystem. It provides an event-driven, cached view of cluster state, replacing naive polling with efficient watch-based synchronization.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `tools/cache/reflector.go`: `Reflector` performs `LIST` to obtain a snapshot, then watches for subsequent changes.\n- `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`: `DeltaFIFO` queues delta events (Add, Update, Delete) keyed by object.\n- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go`: `SharedInformer` coordinates reflector, store, and event handler dispatch.\n- `tools/cache/index.go`: Thread-safe indexing for fast lookups by non-key fields (e.g., by owner reference, node name).\n- `informers/factory.go`: `SharedInformerFactory` creates and coordinates informers for multiple resource types.\n\n**Data Flow (Simplified)**:\n\n```\nKubernetes API Server (LIST/WATCH)\n        ↓\n    Reflector (ListerWatcher interface)\n        ↓\n    DeltaFIFO (queues Add, Update, Delete, Sync deltas)\n        ↓\n  Indexer (in-process cache, thread-safe store)\n        ↓\n  Event Handlers (onAdd, onUpdate, onDelete → enqueue to work queue)\n        ↓\n  Work Queue (rate-limited, deduplicates, allows retries)\n        ↓\n  Controller Business Logic (reconciliation)\n```\n\n**Reflector Behavior**:\n- Calls `ListerWatcher.List(options)` with a `limit` to retrieve objects page-by-page.\n- Stores the returned `resourceVersion`.\n- Calls `ListerWatcher.Watch(from resourceVersion)` to stream subsequent changes.\n- If the watch stream ends, Reflector retries with backoff. If the apiserver says the resourceVersion is \"too old,\" Reflector re-lists with the latest resourceVersion.\n- Watch bookmarks (special events without object mutations) update the Reflector's resourceVersion, enabling efficient recovery.\n\n**DeltaFIFO Semantics**:\n- Accumulates deltas (not individual events) for each object key.\n- Deduplicates: if an object is added multiple times before being popped, it appears once with all accumulated deltas.\n- Supports \"Replace\" semantics: when the full list is refreshed, objects not in the new list are deleted from the cache.\n\n**Shared Indexer (Thread-Safety)**:\n- The `Indexer` is a thread-safe map of object keys to objects, with secondary indexes (e.g., by label selectors, field selectors, owner references).\n- Controllers query the indexer via `Lister` (read-only) interfaces, avoiding direct cache access.\n\n**Informer Lifecycle**:\n1. **Creation**: `factory.Apps().V1().Deployments()` returns a `DeploymentInformer` wrapping a `SharedInformer`.\n2. **Registration**: Controllers call `informer.Informer().AddEventHandler()` or `informer.Informer().AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod()` to register callbacks.\n3. **Start**: `factory.Start(ctx)` spawns goroutines for each informer's Reflector and processes pending deltas.\n4. **Synchronization**: `factory.WaitForCacheSync(ctx)` blocks until all informers have listed their initial state.\n5. **Shutdown**: `factory.Shutdown()` gracefully stops all informers.\n\n### 2.7 Listers (`listers/`)\n\nListers provide read-only, typed access to the informer cache.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `listers/*/`: Auto-generated typed listers (e.g., `listers/apps/v1/deployment_lister.go`).\n- `tools/cache/listers.go`: Base lister interfaces and helpers.\n\n**Design Pattern**:\n```go\ntype DeploymentLister interface {\n    List(selector labels.Selector) ([]*appsv1.Deployment, error)\n    Deployments(namespace string) DeploymentNamespaceLister\n}\n\ntype DeploymentNamespaceLister interface {\n    Get(name string) (*appsv1.Deployment, error)\n    List(selector labels.Selector) ([]*appsv1.Deployment, error)\n}\n```\n\nListers use the informer's indexer to answer queries without polling the apiserver. For example, `deploymentLister.Deployments(\"default\").Get(\"my-deploy\")` is a cache lookup, not an API call.\n\n**Caveat**: The lister's data is eventually consistent. If a controller writes an object and immediately reads it back, the cache might lag.\n\n### 2.8 Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)\n\nWork queues decouple event detection (informer) from reconciliation (controller), enabling:\n- Rate limiting (exponential backoff per item).\n- Deduplication (if an item is enqueued multiple times, it's processed once).\n- Retries on failure.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `util/workqueue/queue.go`: `TypedInterface[T]` (generic queue interface) and `TypedRateLimitingInterface[T]` (rate-limited variant).\n- `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go`: Delayed queue requeuing items after a backoff period.\n- `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go`: Combines delay and rate limiting.\n- `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`: Exponential failure rate limiter, bucket rate limiter, max-of combinators.\n\n**Controller Loop Pattern**:\n```go\nfor {\n    item, shutdown := queue.Get()\n    if shutdown { break }\n\n    err := controller.reconcile(item)\n    if err != nil {\n        queue.AddRateLimited(item)  // Retry with backoff\n    } else {\n        queue.Forget(item)  // Reset backoff on success\n    }\n    queue.Done(item)\n}\n```\n\n**Rate Limiting Strategies**:\n- **Exponential Backoff**: Delay increases exponentially after each failure (e.g., 5ms → 50ms → 500ms → capped).\n- **Token Bucket**: A configured rate (e.g., 50 items/sec) with burst allowance.\n- **MaxOf**: Combines multiple limiters, using the most conservative delay.\n\n### 2.9 Leader Election (`tools/leaderelection/`)\n\nIn a replicated controller setup (multiple instances for HA), leader election ensures only one instance is \"leading\" (reconciling objects).\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`: `LeaderElector` and `LeaderElectionConfig`.\n- `tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/`: Implementations of locks backed by Lease, ConfigMap, or Endpoints objects.\n\n**Mechanism**:\n- Multiple candidate replicas compete to update a shared `Lease` object (in a configurable namespace, e.g., `kube-system`).\n- The replica with the newest lease timestamp is the leader.\n- Each leader periodically renews the lease; if it fails to renew before `LeaseDuration`, another replica can take over.\n- Callbacks (`OnStartedLeading`, `OnStoppedLeading`) notify the controller of leadership transitions.\n\n**Configuration Parameters**:\n- `LeaseDuration`: How long the lease is valid (e.g., 60s).\n- `RenewDeadline`: How long the leader waits before giving up renewal (e.g., 40s).\n- `RetryPeriod`: How often non-leaders retry acquiring the lease (e.g., 2s).\n\n**Clock Skew Tolerance**: The implementation is tolerant to clock drift between nodes because it compares local time to the last observation of the shared lease. However, large clock skew rates can cause frequent leadership flaps.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 API Access Flow (Configuration → HTTP)\n\n**Scenario**: A controller reads a Pod from the cluster.\n\n**File Path Evidence**:\n\n1. **Configuration Loading** (`rest/config.go`, `tools/clientcmd/`):\n   - Call `clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(kubeconfig, context)` or `rest.InClusterConfig()`.\n   - Returns a `rest.Config` with `.Host`, `.BearerToken`, `.TLSClientConfig`, `.QPS`, `.Burst`.\n\n2. **REST Client Construction** (`rest/config.go`):\n   - Call `rest.NewForConfig(config)` → `newRESTClient(config)` → constructs `RESTClient` with:\n     - Base URL and API path.\n     - HTTP client via `HTTPClientFor(config)` (applies TLS, auth, transport wrappers).\n     - Rate limiter via `config.RateLimiter` or default token bucket.\n\n3. **Typed Client Creation** (`kubernetes/clientset.go`):\n   - Call `kubernetes.NewForConfig(restConfig)` → returns `Clientset`.\n   - The Clientset holds references to versioned client factories (e.g., `CoreV1Client`).\n\n4. **Request Building** (`rest/request.go`, `kubernetes/typed/core/v1/pod.go`):\n   ```go\n   pod, err := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", v1.GetOptions{})\n   ```\n   - Internally invokes:\n   ```go\n   client.Verb(\"GET\").\n       Prefix(\"api\", \"v1\").\n       Namespace(\"default\").\n       Resource(\"pods\").\n       Name(\"my-pod\").\n       Into(&pod).Do(ctx)\n   ```\n\n5. **HTTP Request Execution** (`rest/request.go`, `rest/client.go`):\n   - `Request.Do(ctx)` constructs the full HTTP request:\n     - Verb: `GET`\n     - URL: `https://apiserver:6443/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod`\n     - Headers: `Authorization: Bearer <token>`, `Accept: application/json`, `User-Agent: client-go/v0.x.y`\n   - Applies rate limiting: waits if token bucket is exhausted.\n   - Calls the transport chain (auth, TLS, custom wrappers).\n   - Issues the HTTP request.\n\n6. **Response Handling** (`rest/request.go`):\n   - Checks HTTP status code.\n   - If 2xx: deserializes JSON/Protobuf into the target object.\n   - If non-2xx: deserializes `metav1.Status` and wraps in `errors.StatusError` (allows `errors.IsNotFound()`, `errors.IsConflict()`, etc.).\n   - If 429: reads `Retry-After`, waits, and retries.\n\n**File Map for This Flow**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/config.go` — Configuration struct and loading logic.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/client.go` — RESTClient struct and base HTTP client setup.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/request.go` — Request builder and execution.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/clientset.go` — Clientset factory.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/core/v1/pod.go` — Typed Pod client (generated).\n\n### 3.2 Informer and Controller Loop Flow\n\n**Scenario**: A controller reconciles Deployments by watching for changes and managing Pods.\n\n**File Path Evidence**:\n\n1. **Informer Factory Setup** (`informers/factory.go`):\n   ```go\n   factory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 30*time.Second)\n   deploymentInformer := factory.Apps().V1().Deployments()\n   podInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods()\n   ```\n   - `factory.go` creates a `sharedInformerFactory` struct holding a Clientset and resource-specific informer caches.\n   - Each informer wraps a `SharedInformer` (from `tools/cache/shared_informer.go`).\n\n2. **Event Handler Registration** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`, sample in `sample-controller/controller.go`):\n   ```go\n   deploymentInformer.Informer().AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n       AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n           controller.enqueueDeployment(obj)\n       },\n       UpdateFunc: func(old, new interface{}) {\n           controller.enqueueDeployment(new)\n       },\n       DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n           controller.enqueueDeployment(obj)\n       },\n   })\n   ```\n\n3. **Informer Startup** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`, `tools/cache/reflector.go`):\n   - `factory.Start(ctx)` spawns goroutines for each informer's Reflector and cache populator.\n   - For each informer:\n     - `Reflector.ListAndWatch()` is called in a goroutine.\n     - Reflector calls `ListerWatcher.List(options)` (from the typed client, e.g., `clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"\").List(ctx, ...)`).\n     - Reflector receives a list of Deployments and stores the resourceVersion (e.g., \"12345\").\n     - Reflector calls `ListerWatcher.Watch(options)` with `resourceVersion=12345`.\n     - Watch returns a channel of `watch.Event` objects.\n\n4. **Watch Stream Processing** (`tools/cache/reflector.go`, `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`):\n   - Each watch event is converted to a Delta (Add, Update, Delete, Sync) and pushed into DeltaFIFO.\n   - Example: If a Deployment is updated, a `Modified` delta is enqueued for that Deployment's key (e.g., `\"default/my-deployment\"`).\n\n5. **Cache Population** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`, `tools/cache/controller.go`):\n   - A separate goroutine runs `sharedIndexInformer.controller.Run()` in a loop.\n   - It calls `DeltaFIFO.Pop()` to retrieve accumulated deltas for a key.\n   - It updates the Indexer (thread-safe cache) with the latest object state.\n   - It triggers registered event handlers (`OnAdd`, `OnUpdate`, `OnDelete`).\n\n6. **Event Handler and Work Queue** (`sample-controller/controller.go`):\n   ```go\n   func (c *Controller) enqueueDeployment(obj interface{}) {\n       key, err := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n       if err != nil { return }\n       c.workqueue.Add(key)  // Enqueue as string \"namespace/name\"\n   }\n   ```\n   - The event handler extracts the object's key and enqueues it to the work queue.\n   - The work queue uses rate limiting to prevent overwhelming the controller.\n\n7. **Controller Reconciliation Loop** (`sample-controller/controller.go`):\n   ```go\n   func (c *Controller) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int) {\n       defer c.workqueue.ShutDown()\n\n       // Wait for cache sync\n       if !cache.WaitForCacheSync(ctx.Done(), c.deploymentsSynced, c.podsSynced) {\n           return\n       }\n\n       // Start worker goroutines\n       for i := 0; i < workers; i++ {\n           go wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, c.runWorker, time.Second)\n       }\n\n       <-ctx.Done()\n   }\n\n   func (c *Controller) runWorker(ctx context.Context) {\n       for c.processNextWorkItem(ctx) {}\n   }\n\n   func (c *Controller) processNextWorkItem(ctx context.Context) bool {\n       item, shutdown := c.workqueue.Get()\n       if shutdown { return false }\n       defer c.workqueue.Done(item)\n\n       key := item.(string)\n       err := c.reconcile(ctx, key)\n\n       if err != nil {\n           c.workqueue.AddRateLimited(item)\n       } else {\n           c.workqueue.Forget(item)\n       }\n       return true\n   }\n\n   func (c *Controller) reconcile(ctx context.Context, key string) error {\n       // Parse key \"namespace/name\"\n       namespace, name, _ := cache.SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)\n\n       // Read from cache (not API)\n       deployment, err := c.deploymentsLister.Deployments(namespace).Get(name)\n       if errors.IsNotFound(err) { return nil }  // Already deleted\n\n       // Business logic: ensure Deployment has desired Pods\n       desiredReplicas := *deployment.Spec.Replicas\n       actualPods, err := c.podsLister.Pods(namespace).List(labels.SelectorFromSet(deployment.Spec.Selector.MatchLabels))\n\n       if len(actualPods) < desiredReplicas {\n           // Create missing Pods via API\n           pod := &corev1.Pod{...}\n           _, err := c.kubeclientset.CoreV1().Pods(namespace).Create(ctx, pod, v1.CreateOptions{})\n       }\n\n       return err\n   }\n   ```\n\n**Key Observations**:\n- The controller reads from the cache (via listers) for fast, non-blocking queries.\n- The controller writes to the API server for state mutations (creating/updating/deleting objects).\n- If reconciliation fails, the work queue's rate limiter ensures exponential backoff before the next retry.\n- All event handler callbacks run sequentially per handler; the work queue enables concurrent reconciliation.\n\n**File Map for This Flow**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/factory.go` — Factory for creating and starting informers.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go` — Core informer coordination logic.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go` — LIST/WATCH implementation.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` — Delta queue for deduplication.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/controller.go` — Low-level controller coordinating Reflector and cache update.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/index.go` — Thread-safe indexer.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/queue.go`, `rate_limiting_queue.go` — Work queue and rate limiting.\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go` — Example controller using the above.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Watch Stream Disruption and Resilience\n\n**Failure Mode**: The apiserver closes the watch connection unexpectedly (network glitch, apiserver restart, kubelet drain).\n\n**Reflector Recovery** (`tools/cache/reflector.go`):\n- When the watch stream ends, `Reflector.ListAndWatch()` retries with exponential backoff.\n- If the previous resourceVersion is too old (apiserver has garbage-collected older events), the Reflector re-lists from the latest resourceVersion, avoiding the \"too old\" error.\n- Watch bookmarks (heartbeat events) allow the Reflector to update its resourceVersion without object mutations, enabling faster recovery on reconnection.\n- **Trade-off**: Recovery takes time (configurable via `minWatchTimeout`, default 5 minutes for watch list timeouts). During outages, the controller's cache may lag.\n\n### 4.2 Cache Coherency and Eventual Consistency\n\n**Limitation**: The informer cache is eventually consistent. A controller may not immediately observe an object it just created.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\npod, _ := c.podClient.Create(ctx, &pod, v1.CreateOptions{})\n// Immediately after, the lister might NOT have this pod\npodFromCache, _ := c.podsLister.Pods(namespace).Get(pod.Name)  // Might fail\n```\n\n**Reasons**:\n- The apiserver's response doesn't guarantee the object is in the watch stream yet.\n- The Reflector's watch stream may lag (network latency, backpressure in the event queue).\n- The `DeltaFIFO` may accumulate multiple events before the cache is updated.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Controllers check the API directly for critical reads after writes: `client.Get(ctx, key, ...)`.\n- Use `resourceVersion` matching to ensure linearizability: `pod, _ := c.podClient.Get(ctx, name, v1.GetOptions{ResourceVersion: returnedPod.ResourceVersion})`.\n- Set event handler resync periods appropriately (default 30 seconds) to force periodic full reconciliations.\n\n### 4.3 Rate Limiting and Backpressure\n\n**Limit**: The client's token bucket rate limiter is enforced at request time, not globally. If multiple workers are enqueuing items, they might still exceed the QPS if they all call `Get()` simultaneously.\n\n**Constraint**: The apiserver has its own rate limits (API Priority and Fairness). If a client exceeds the server's limit, it receives HTTP `429 Too Many Requests`.\n\n**Handling** (`rest/with_retry.go`):\n- The client automatically retries `429` responses, reading the `Retry-After` header and sleeping.\n- The work queue's rate limiter is separate from the HTTP client's rate limiting; both operate independently, leading to layered backpressure.\n\n### 4.4 Memory Overhead of Informers\n\n**Concern**: An informer caches the entire resource collection in memory. For large clusters with millions of objects, this becomes prohibitive.\n\n**Mitigation Strategies**:\n- **Namespace-Scoped Informers**: Use `informers.NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions(clientset, resync, informers.WithNamespace(namespace))` to cache only objects in a specific namespace.\n- **Label/Field Selectors**: Pass `tweakListOptions` to filter objects: `informers.WithTweakListOptions(func(opts *v1.ListOptions) { opts.LabelSelector = \"app=my-app\" })`.\n- **Custom Transforms**: Apply `WithTransform()` to strip unnecessary fields (e.g., managed fields, annotations) from cached objects.\n\n**Trade-off**: Reduced scope means the controller cannot observe cross-namespace relationships without separate API calls.\n\n### 4.5 Resync Period and Duplicate Events\n\n**Behavior**: Periodically (every `resyncPeriod`), the Reflector sends a synthetic `Sync` delta for every object in the cache, even if unchanged.\n\n**Purpose**: Ensures stale event handlers see all objects again, triggering reconciliation even if the watch stream missed an update.\n\n**Cost**: If `resyncPeriod` is too short, the controller receives many redundant events, increasing load. If too long, stale issues take longer to surface.\n\n**Guidance**: Default 30 seconds is suitable for most controllers. Custom resync periods can be set per informer type via `WithCustomResyncConfig()`.\n\n### 4.6 Leader Election Clock Skew\n\n**Failure Mode**: Nodes have significantly drifted clocks (e.g., +30 seconds on one node, -30 seconds on another). Multiple replicas might believe they are the leader simultaneously, causing conflicting writes.\n\n**Mitigation** (`tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`):\n- The implementation tolerates clock skew by comparing local time to the last observed lease timestamp (not the lease timestamp itself).\n- However, if clock drift exceeds a certain ratio, leadership transitions become unstable (high flapping).\n- **Recommendation**: Keep clock skew < 100 milliseconds using NTP or similar. Configure `LeaseDuration / RenewDeadline` ratio to match expected skew tolerance.\n\n### 4.7 Serialization Overhead\n\n**Trade-off**: Protobuf is more efficient than JSON in terms of bandwidth and parsing time, but requires compiled schema definitions.\n\n**Default**: Client-go uses JSON by default. To enable Protobuf:\n- For typed clients: code generation can produce clients preferring Protobuf via `--prefers-protobuf` flag.\n- For requests: call `request.UseProtobufAsDefault()` on each request.\n- **Cost**: Protobuf requires the apiserver to return Protobuf-encoded responses; not all API versions support it equally.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization\n\n### 5.1 Custom Informer Factories\n\nControllers can extend `SharedInformerFactory` to add custom informers for CRDs.\n\n**Pattern** (`sample-controller/pkg/generated/informers/`):\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Foos() FooInformer\n}\n\ntype fooInformer struct {\n    factory internalinterfaces.SharedInformerFactory\n    namespace string\n}\n\nfunc (f *fooInformer) Informer() cache.SharedIndexInformer {\n    return f.factory.InformerFor(&samplev1alpha1.Foo{}, &fooInformer{})\n}\n```\n\n**Extension**: A controller with custom types (e.g., CRDs) can use `code-generator` to produce typed informers, or manually implement the factory interface and call `factory.InformerFor()` with the custom type.\n\n### 5.2 Event Handler Registration and Custom Logic\n\nEvent handlers are invoked synchronously per handler, so blocking or expensive operations should be offloaded to a work queue.\n\n**Anti-Pattern**:\n```go\ninformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        // Heavy reconciliation logic here\n        // Blocks the event stream!\n    },\n})\n```\n\n**Best Practice**:\n```go\ninformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        key, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n        c.workqueue.Add(key)  // Fast, non-blocking\n    },\n})\n// ... reconciliation happens asynchronously in worker goroutines.\n```\n\n### 5.3 Custom Rate Limiters\n\nThe work queue allows pluggable rate limiters via `workqueue.NewTypedRateLimitingQueue()`.\n\n**Example** (`sample-controller/controller.go`):\n```go\nratelimiter := workqueue.NewTypedMaxOfRateLimiter(\n    workqueue.NewTypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter[cache.ObjectName](5*time.Millisecond, 1000*time.Second),\n    &workqueue.TypedBucketRateLimiter[cache.ObjectName]{Limiter: rate.NewLimiter(50, 300)},\n)\nqueue := workqueue.NewTypedRateLimitingQueue(ratelimiter)\n```\n\nThis combines exponential backoff (per item) with a token bucket (global rate). A controller can implement `RateLimiter` to enforce custom backoff strategies (e.g., exponential with jitter, priority-based delays).\n\n### 5.4 Transport Wrappers and Custom Middleware\n\n`rest.Config.WrapTransport()` allows layering custom `http.RoundTripper` middleware.\n\n**Example**: Add request tracing, custom headers, or circuit-breaker logic.\n```go\nconfig.WrapTransport = func(rt http.RoundTripper) http.RoundTripper {\n    return &customTransport{rt: rt}\n}\n\ntype customTransport struct {\n    rt http.RoundTripper\n}\n\nfunc (ct *customTransport) RoundTrip(req *http.Request) (*http.Response, error) {\n    // Custom logic: add headers, trace, check circuit breaker\n    req.Header.Set(\"X-Custom-Header\", \"value\")\n    return ct.rt.RoundTrip(req)\n}\n```\n\n### 5.5 Custom Serializers and Content Types\n\nAdvanced use cases may need to support custom wire formats (e.g., YAML, MessagePack). This is done by implementing the `runtime.Serializer` interface and setting it on `rest.Config.ContentConfig.Negotiator`.\n\n**Risk**: Non-standard formats may not be compatible with all Kubernetes tooling.\n\n### 5.6 Server-Side Apply (SSA) and ApplyConfigurations\n\nFor declarative object management, `applyconfigurations/` provides type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\ndeployment := appsv1apply.Deployment(\"my-dep\", \"default\").\n    WithSpec(appsv1apply.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(3).\n        WithSelector(metav1apply.LabelSelector().WithMatchLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"foo\"})))\n\nresult, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Apply(ctx, deployment, v1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"})\n```\n\n**Advantage**: SSA prevents conflicts when multiple controllers co-manage the same object (e.g., multiple operators adding fields to the same Deployment).\n\n**Trade-off**: Requires understanding of field ownership tracking and field managers.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Latency**:\n- **Cache Hit**: Lister queries return in microseconds (in-memory hash map lookup).\n- **API Call**: Direct client calls incur network latency (typically 10-100ms for in-cluster communication).\n- **Watch Stream**: Events typically arrive within 1-2 seconds of object mutation in the apiserver.\n\n**Throughput**:\n- A single work queue worker can reconcile ~100-1000 objects per second (depending on reconciliation complexity).\n- Multiple workers scale linearly (up to OS thread limits and apiserver rate limits).\n\n**Memory**:\n- An informer caches one copy of each object (plus secondary indexes). For 10,000 Pods (~100 KB each), expect ~1 GB overhead.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and High Availability\n\n**Failure Scenarios**:\n1. **API Server Down**: Controllers continue running (cache intact) but cannot write changes. On recovery, the controller resumes normal operation.\n2. **Controller Crash**: Kubernetes restarts the Pod. The informer re-syncs from the apiserver. Work queue items are lost (unless persisted externally).\n3. **Replica Controller Down (in HA setup)**: Other replicas assume leadership (via lease election) and take over reconciliation. Failover takes ~10-60 seconds (configurable via lease parameters).\n\n**Best Practices**:\n- Run controllers in Deployments with multiple replicas for redundancy.\n- Use leader election to prevent duplicate work and write conflicts.\n- Monitor watch stream errors and reconciliation latency via metrics.\n- Set informer resync periods to force periodic full reconciliations (mitigates watch stream gaps).\n\n### 6.3 Observability and Debugging\n\n**Metrics** (`tools/metrics/`):\n- Informer metrics: list duration, watch events per second, cache size.\n- Work queue metrics: queue depth, processing latency, retries.\n- HTTP client metrics: request latency, status codes, throttling events.\n\n**Logging**:\n- Use klog (the Kubernetes logging library) with verbosity levels:\n  - `klog.V(4).Info(...)` for debug-level details (informer event processing, request building).\n  - `klog.V(2).Info(...)` for general events (cache sync, worker loop).\n  - `klog.Error(...)` for errors.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nreflector.SetReporter(&metrics.DefaultReflectorMetricsFactory{})\n// Metrics are exported to /metrics endpoint (Prometheus format)\n```\n\n**Common Issues**:\n- **High watch error rate**: Check network stability between controller and apiserver.\n- **Large work queue depth**: Controller reconciliation is slow; consider scaling worker count or optimizing reconciliation logic.\n- **Cache not syncing**: Verify Reflector.ListAndWatch() is running; check informer startup and WaitForCacheSync() timeout.\n\n### 6.4 Security Implications\n\n**Authentication and RBAC**:\n- Client-go respects Kubernetes RBAC. If a service account lacks permission to read Deployments, `informer.Lister().List()` will fail on first access.\n- Prefer minimal RBAC roles (only grant permissions the controller needs).\n\n**Impersonation**:\n- A controller can use `config.Impersonate` to operate on behalf of another user (if authorized by RBAC).\n- Use with caution; audit logs will show the impersonated user, not the actual service account.\n\n**Token Refresh**:\n- In-cluster tokens are auto-refreshed by the kubelet. Out-of-cluster clients must handle token rotation manually or via auth plugins.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directories Map\n\n| Component | Key Files | Purpose |\n|-----------|-----------|---------|\n| **REST Client** | `rest/config.go`, `rest/client.go`, `rest/request.go` | Configuration loading, HTTP client, request builder |\n| **Transport & Auth** | `rest/transport.go`, `transport/` (in k8s.io/transport) | TLS, authentication plugins, RoundTripper chain |\n| **Typed Clients** | `kubernetes/clientset.go`, `kubernetes/typed/*/` | Generated type-safe API clients |\n| **Dynamic Client** | `dynamic/interface.go`, `dynamic/simple.go` | Untyped client for CRDs and arbitrary resources |\n| **Discovery** | `discovery/discovery_client.go`, `discovery/cached_discovery.go` | API resource enumeration, schema introspection |\n| **Informers** | `informers/factory.go`, `informers/*/` | Informer factories for all API types (auto-generated) |\n| **Core Cache** | `tools/cache/reflector.go`, `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`, `tools/cache/shared_informer.go` | LIST/WATCH, delta queue, event dispatch |\n| **Indexing** | `tools/cache/index.go`, `tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go` | Thread-safe cache with secondary indexes |\n| **Listers** | `listers/*/` | Read-only, typed cache accessors (auto-generated) |\n| **Work Queue** | `util/workqueue/queue.go`, `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go` | Deduplication, rate limiting, retries |\n| **Leader Election** | `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`, `tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/` | HA coordination via shared locks |\n| **Event Recording** | `tools/record/` | Recording events to apiserver (event broadcaster) |\n| **Example Controller** | `sample-controller/controller.go` | Full example demonstrating informer and controller patterns |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Conclusion\n\nClient-go's architecture elegantly separates concerns: configuration and authentication (boundary with kubeconfig), REST transport (HTTP layer), type-safe or dynamic API clients (user-facing), event-driven informers (efficient caching), and work queues (resilient reconciliation). The eventual consistency model trades immediate coherency for resilience and scalability. Controllers built with client-go are event-driven, not polling-based, and can safely operate in multi-replica setups via leader election.\n\nUnderstanding the interaction between Reflector (LIST/WATCH), DeltaFIFO (deduplication), Indexer (cache), event handlers (enqueue), and work queue (reconciliation) is critical for building robust controllers. Extension points (custom rate limiters, transport wrappers, informer factories) allow fine-grained control over behavior. Operational considerations—cache memory overhead, watch stream resilience, clock skew in leader election, and observability via metrics—are essential for production deployments.\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3693,"cache_read_input_tokens":81634,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3693},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"bcb00934-5194-4a60-bab0-f0466bc891a9","uuid":"9337bc3e-27bc-4139-93d8-7edb41d696c5"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01JexWg5ZLf1a6JTZzg3HRUV","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/documentation.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"bcb00934-5194-4a60-bab0-f0466bc891a9","uuid":"95575f0a-d8bd-4c7e-a6e9-bba545821a9e","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Client-go Systems Guide: Advanced Architecture and Operations\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nClient-go is the fundamental Go client library for Kubernetes API interaction and controller development. It abstracts HTTP communication with the Kubernetes API server into a layered architecture comprising four key subsystems: (1) REST-based API access with content negotiation and rate limiting, (2) type-safe clients for built-in APIs (kubernetes.Clientset) and dynamic untyped clients for CRDs, (3) a caching and event-driven informer system powered by watch-based state synchronization, and (4) a work queue and leader election infrastructure for building resilient, distributed controllers. This guide explains the architecture, component interactions, end-to-end control flows, operational tradeoffs, and extension patterns essential for building robust Kubernetes controllers and integrating with the API server.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### 1.1 Purpose and Scope\n\nClient-go serves as the canonical Go library for interacting with Kubernetes clusters. Its core mandate is twofold:\n\n1. **API Access Layer**: Provide a safe, type-checked, and performant interface to the Kubernetes REST API.\n2. **Controller Infrastructure**: Supply the event-driven machinery and tools necessary to build stateful, resilient controllers that manage Kubernetes objects declaratively.\n\nClient-go is positioned between two critical boundaries:\n\n- **Upstream Boundary (Kubernetes API Server)**: Client-go communicates with the apiserver over HTTP/2, consuming `LIST`, `WATCH`, `GET`, `POST`, `PATCH`, and `DELETE` operations. It must handle the apiserver's versioning, deprecation, resource discovery, and rate-limit signals (HTTP `429` with `Retry-After` headers).\n- **Downstream Boundary (Controllers and Tools)**: Controllers, kubectl, kubelets, and custom clients consume client-go's high-level abstractions (Clientsets, Informers, Listers, Work Queues) to interact with Kubernetes state without directly managing HTTP, serialization, or polling logic.\n\n### 1.2 External Dependencies\n\n- **k8s.io/apimachinery**: Core Kubernetes type system, serialization (JSON/Protobuf/CBOR), resource versioning, and the Watch interface.\n- **k8s.io/api**: Kubernetes built-in API types (e.g., Pod, Deployment, Service).\n- **Go standard library**: HTTP client, reflection, channels, sync primitives (mutex, WaitGroup).\n- **Third-party libraries**: OpenAPI schema handling, rate limiting (golang.org/x/time/rate), protobuf serialization.\n\n### 1.3 Architectural Principles\n\nClient-go's design reflects several key principles:\n\n- **Code Generation for Type Safety**: Typed clients, listers, and informers are generated from API type definitions, enabling compile-time safety while reducing manual boilerplate.\n- **Eventual Consistency Model**: The informer cache is eventually consistent with the apiserver; consistency is traded for scalability and resilience to transient network failures.\n- **Decoupled Event Detection from Reconciliation**: Informer event handlers (fast, non-blocking) enqueue work items; a separate work queue allows controllers to reconcile asynchronously with exponential backoff.\n- **Single-Writer Semantics**: Leader election ensures only one controller instance acts as \"leader,\" preventing conflicting writes in a high-availability setup.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 REST Client Subsystem (`rest/`)\n\nThe REST client is the foundational transport layer. All higher-level clients ultimately use `rest.Client` and `rest.Request` for HTTP communication.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `rest/config.go`: `Config` struct holds server address, authentication credentials, TLS settings, QPS/Burst rate limiting, and custom transport wrappers.\n- `rest/client.go`: `RESTClient` encapsulates base URL, API path, negotiated serializer, backoff manager, and rate limiter.\n- `rest/request.go`: `Request` struct implements a fluent builder pattern for constructing requests (`.Verb()`, `.Resource()`, `.Namespace()`, `.Name()`, `.Into()`, `.Do()`).\n- `rest/transport.go`: `TransportFor()` constructs an `http.RoundTripper` chain layering authentication, TLS, compression, and rate limiting.\n\n**Key Concepts**:\n\n1. **Builder Pattern for Requests**: A single `Request` instance defers response processing until `.Do()` or `.Into()` is called, decoupling request assembly from execution.\n   ```\n   client.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", v1.GetOptions{})\n   // Internally translates to:\n   // GET /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod\n   ```\n\n2. **Content Negotiation**: The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate wire format (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR). Optional Accept custom parameters enable metadata-only retrieval (`as=PartialObjectMetadata`) or table-formatted lists (`as=Table`).\n\n3. **Transport Chain (RoundTrippers)**: The `http.RoundTripper` interface allows layered middleware:\n   - Authentication (Bearer token, client certs, OAuth via plugins)\n   - TLS/mTLS configuration\n   - Compression (gzip)\n   - User-Agent and custom header injection\n   - Impersonation (user/group override)\n\n4. **Rate Limiting and Backoff**:\n   - **Client-side**: `Config.QPS` (default 5) and `Config.Burst` (default 10) define a token bucket rate limiter enforced at request time.\n   - **Server-side**: The apiserver may return HTTP `429 Too Many Requests`. The client's default transport reads the `Retry-After` header and automatically retries with exponential backoff (capped at 1000 seconds).\n\n### 2.2 Configuration and Authentication (`rest/config.go`, `tools/clientcmd/`)\n\nLoading cluster credentials and constructing a `rest.Config` is logically separated from using it.\n\n**Core Files**:\n- `rest/config.go`: `Config` struct and
